BMC Plant Biol. 11, 24 (2011)." href="/articles/s41598-019-47985-w#ref-CR50" id="ref-link-section-d25187e2602">50</a></sup>.</p><p>Fruits, like other aerial plant parts, are coated with a lipophilic cuticle largely composed of waxes and cutin, which impacts many pre- and post- harvest processes including fruit water relations, expansion and the response to biotic and abiotic stresses<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 38" title="Yeats, T. H. et al. The identification of cutin synthase: formation of the plant polyester cutin. Nat. Chem. Biol. 8, 609â11 (2012)." href="/articles/s41598-019-47985-w#ref-CR38" id="ref-link-section-d25187e2609">38</a></sup>. Our data indicate that structural and regulatory genes controlling cuticle biosynthesis in tomato and/or Arabidopsis also showed skin-enriched expression in eggplant fruits, suggesting that the underlyingÂ regulatory network is highly conserved in eudicots.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec11">Fruit development and ripening</h3><p>Tomato, eggplant and pepper fruits undergo physiological changes during ripening, which are ethylene-dependent in tomato and ethylene-independent in eggplant and pepper. Ripening of the tomato fruit is well studied, and is controlled by a complex signal transduction pathway, involving several transcriptional regulators<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 32" title="Vrebalov, J. et al. A MADS-box gene necessary for fruit ripening at the tomato ripening-inhibitor (rin) locus. Science 296, 343â6 (2002)." href="/articles/s41598-019-47985-w#ref-CR32" id="ref-link-section-d25187e2621">32</a></sup>. Our transcriptional and co-expression studies suggest that more similarities than differences exist in the mechanisms controlling fruit ripening in different Solanaceae clades. The mRNAs encoding known regulators of ripening are upregulated during ripening in tomato, eggplant and pepper, with the exception of the <i>CNR</i> gene<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 51" title="Manning, K. et al. A naturally occurring epigenetic mutation in a gene encoding an SBP-box transcription factor inhibits tomato fruit ripening. Nat. Genet. 38, 948â952 (2006)." href="/articles/s41598-019-47985-w#ref-CR51" id="ref-link-section-d25187e2628">51</a></sup>, which is upregulated in climacteric tomato, but not in non-climacteric eggplant and pepper fruits. This observation partially contrasts with the proposed role of <i>CNR</i> in regulating ripening upstream of ethylene synthesis<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 52" title="Adams-Phillips, L., Barry, C. &amp; Giovannoni, J. Signal transduction systems regulating fruit ripening. Trends Plant Sci. 9, 331â338 (2004)." href="/articles/s41598-019-47985-w#ref-CR52" id="ref-link-section-d25187e2635">52</a></sup>. With the exception of <i>CNR</i>, the main ripening regulators appear to be regulated in a similar fashion in climacteric and non-climacteric fruits, and they also appear to have similar functions, as highlighted by the very similar developmental phenotypes obtained by ectopic expression of the <i>TAGL1</i> transcription factor in tomato and eggplant.</p><p>The main components of the network controlling fleshy fruit ripening across different Solanaceae include members of the ethylene receptor gene family, as well as <i>ETHYLENE</i> and <i>AUXIN RESPONSE FACTORS</i> (<i>ERF</i>s and <i>ARF</i>s) in both climacteric and non-climacteric fruits. Apart from <i>CNR</i>, the genes showing different regulation in climacteric versus non-climacteric fruits are those involved in ethylene biosynthesis (<i>ACS</i> and, to a lesser extent, <i>ACO</i>). This, together with the fact that climacteric fruit ripening in the Solanaceae is of polyphyletic origin, Â suggests that the twoÂ different types of fruit ripening arose recently during evolution, through a modification in the regulation of relatively few components, including <i>CNR</i> and ethylene biosynthetic genes.</p></div></div></section><section aria-labelledby="Sec12" data-title="Methods"><div class="c-article-section" id="Sec12-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="Sec12">Methods</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="Sec12-content"><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec13">Sequencing, assembly and anchoring</h3><p>The <i>S</i>. <i>melongena</i> 67/3 line was obtained as cross between âPurpuraâ Ã âCIN2â and 305E40 line was derived from the somatic hybridÂ <i>Solanum aethiopicum</i> gr. Gilo(+)<i>S</i>. <i>melongena</i> cv. Dourga, F5 and F6 progenies were derived from the cross between this two lines, 305E40 as female parent and 67/3 as male parent. High molecular weight nuclear DNA was extracted from leaf tissue of young plants according to Carrier <i>et al</i>.<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 53" title="Carrier, G. et al. An efficient and rapid protocol for plant nuclear DNA preparation suitable for next generation sequencing methods. Am. J. Bot. 98, 15â17 (2011)." href="/articles/s41598-019-47985-w#ref-CR53" id="ref-link-section-d25187e2706">53</a></sup> for 67/3 line and using a modified CTAB for lines 305E40 and the RILs population (Supplementary InformationÂ <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41598-019-47985-w#MOESM1">1.1</a>). Small-insert libraries were produced using the TruSeq DNA protocol and long-insert mate-pair libraries were prepared using the Nextera Mate Pair protocol. Libraries were sequenced on an Illumina HiSeq1000 instrument with 2âÃâ100 nt protocol at the Functional Genomics Centre, University of Verona, Italy) (Supplementary InformationÂ <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41598-019-47985-w#MOESM1">1.2</a>). The reads have been submitted to the NCBI Sequence Read Archive under the accession number SRP078398.</p><p>Raw reads underwent a quality filtering process (Supplementary InformationÂ <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41598-019-47985-w#MOESM1">1.3</a>) and error corrected using the SOAP error corrector (V1.00). Assembly and scaffolding were performed using SOAPdenovo2<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 10" title="Luo, R. et al. SOAPdenovo2: an empirically improved memory-efficient short-read de novo assembler. Gigascience 1, 18 (2012)." href="/articles/s41598-019-47985-w#ref-CR10" id="ref-link-section-d25187e2722">10</a></sup> using a multi k-mer strategy. Gaps in scaffolds were filled with GapCloser (Supplementary InformationÂ <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41598-019-47985-w#MOESM1">1.4</a>). Quality of the assembly was assessed by BUSCO v3<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 15" title="SimÃ£o, F. A., Waterhouse, R. M., Ioannidis, P., Kriventseva, E. V &amp; Zdobnov, E. M. BUSCO: assessing genome assembly and annotation completeness with single-copy orthologs. Bioinformatics btv351 (2015)." href="/articles/s41598-019-47985-w#ref-CR15" id="ref-link-section-d25187e2729">15</a></sup> pipeline and by blast search of ESTs downloaded from NCBI (Supplementary InformationÂ <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41598-019-47985-w#MOESM1">1.4</a>). Next-generation genome map of the line â67/3â was performed with BioNano technology at Bionano Genomics (San Diego, California, US), high-molecular-weight DNA was extracted from leaves, labeled and stained using the IrysPrep Kit (Supplementary InformationÂ <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41598-019-47985-w#MOESM1">1.5</a>). Maps were assembled from optical reads with IrysView software (Supplementary InformationÂ <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41598-019-47985-w#MOESM1">1.5</a>) and assembled with Illumina assembly data in hybrid scaffolds using HybridAssembler tool (Supplementary InformationÂ <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41598-019-47985-w#MOESM1">1.5</a>).</p><p>RILs segregation patterns were analyzed with SOILoCo pipeline<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 12" title="Scaglione, D. et al. The genome sequence of the outbreeding globe artichoke constructed de novo incorporating a phase-aware low-pass sequencing strategy of F1 progeny. Sci. Rep. 6, 19427 (2016)." href="/articles/s41598-019-47985-w#ref-CR12" id="ref-link-section-d25187e2749">12</a></sup>, and linkage analysis was performed with âR/qtlâ package<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 54" title="Broman, K. W., Wu, H., Sen, S. &amp; Churchill, G. A. R/qtl: QTL mapping in experimental crosses. Bioinformatics 19, 889â90 (2003)." href="/articles/s41598-019-47985-w#ref-CR54" id="ref-link-section-d25187e2753">54</a></sup> and ordered with Joinmap 4 software<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 55" title="van Ooijen, J. W. JoinMap Â® 4, Software for the calculation of genetic linkage maps in experimental populations. (2006)." href="/articles/s41598-019-47985-w#ref-CR55" id="ref-link-section-d25187e2757">55</a></sup> (Supplementary InformationÂ <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41598-019-47985-w#MOESM1">1.5</a>). Pseudomolecules were obtained by combining both linkage and optical mapping information (Supplementary InformationÂ <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41598-019-47985-w#MOESM1">1.5</a>). A <i>de novo</i> assembly of â305E40â was generated with Abyss<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 56" title="Simpson, J. T. et al. ABySS: a parallel assembler for short read sequence data. Genome Res. 19, 1117â23 (2009)." href="/articles/s41598-019-47985-w#ref-CR56" id="ref-link-section-d25187e2771">56</a></sup> and aligned to â67/3â genome assembly using BLAT<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 57" title="Kent, W. J. BLATâthe BLAST-like alignment tool. Genome Res. 12, 656â64 (2002)." href="/articles/s41598-019-47985-w#ref-CR57" id="ref-link-section-d25187e2775">57</a></sup>.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec14">Transcriptome sequencing, genome annotation and SNP functional classification</h3><p>The 67/3 plants were grown in greenhouse at CREA-GB (Montanaso Lombardo, IT) in standard conditions. RNA from 20 tissues was isolated (TrizolÂ®), directional libraries constructed (Illumina TruSeq Stranded mRNA Library Prep Kit) and sequenced on an Illumina HiSeq. 1000 sequencer. Transcripts were constructed with the Velvetâ+âOases<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 58" title="Schulz, M. H., Zerbino, D. R., Vingron, M. &amp; Birney, E. Oases: Robust de novo RNA-seq assembly across the dynamic range of expression levels. Bioinformatics 28, 1086â1092 (2012)." href="/articles/s41598-019-47985-w#ref-CR58" id="ref-link-section-d25187e2787">58</a></sup> pipeline and EvidentialGene (<a href="http://arthropods.eugenes.org/EvidentialGene/">http://arthropods.eugenes.org/EvidentialGene/</a>). MAKER-P<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 14" title="Campbell, M. S. et al. MAKER-P: a tool kit for the rapid creation, management, and quality control of plant genome annotations. Plant Physiol. 164, 513â24 (2014)." href="/articles/s41598-019-47985-w#ref-CR14" id="ref-link-section-d25187e2798">14</a></sup> pipeline was adopted, and only genes with an AEDââ¤â0.48 were retained, whose quality was evaluated with different pipelines. RNA-Seq reads from each experiment were aligned to the eggplant genome using TopHat 2<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 59" title="Kim, D. et al. Genome Biol. 14, R36 (2013)." href="/articles/s41598-019-47985-w#ref-CR59" id="ref-link-section-d25187e2802">59</a></sup> and expression values (FPKM) for each gene model calculated (Cufflinks 2<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 60" title="Trapnell, C. et al. Transcript assembly and quantification by RNA-Seq reveals unannotated transcripts and isoform switching during cell differentiation. Nat. Biotechnol. 28, 511â5 (2010)." href="/articles/s41598-019-47985-w#ref-CR60" id="ref-link-section-d25187e2806">60</a></sup>). Proteins function assignment was performed with Hmmer<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 61" title="hmmer. Available at: &#xA;                    http://hmmer.janelia.org/&#xA;                    &#xA;                  ." href="/articles/s41598-019-47985-w#ref-CR61" id="ref-link-section-d25187e2811">61</a></sup> and InterProScan<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 62" title="Jones, P. et al. Finally, genetic differences between the reference genome and the â305E40â genotype were evaluated with SnpEff suite<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 63" title="Cingolani, P. et al. Fly (Austin). 6, 80â92 (2012)." href="/articles/s41598-019-47985-w#ref-CR63" id="ref-link-section-d25187e2819">63</a></sup> (Supplementary InformationÂ <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41598-019-47985-w#MOESM1">2.1</a>â<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41598-019-47985-w#MOESM1">2.6</a>).</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec15">Comparative analyses among eggplant, tomato, potato and pepper</h3><p>Eggplant, tomato<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 6" title="The Tomato genome Consortium. The value of nonmodel genomes and an example using SynMap within CoGe to dissect the hexaploidy that predates the Rosids. Trop. Plant Biol. 1, 181â190 (2008)." href="/articles/s41598-019-47985-w#ref-CR69" id="ref-link-section-d25187e2930">69</a></sup> was used to detect orthologous genes among the four species, as well as ohnologs (for dating âTâ triplication<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 6" title="The Tomato genome Consortium. The tomato genome sequence provides insights into fleshy fruit evolution. Nature 485, 635â41 (2012)." href="/articles/s41598-019-47985-w#ref-CR6" id="ref-link-section-d25187e2934">6</a></sup>). Ks-values were calculated for gene pairs using CodeML (PAML package<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 70" title="Yang, Z. PAML 4: phylogenetic analysis by maximum likelihood. Mol. Biol. Evol. 24, 1586â91 (2007)." href="/articles/s41598-019-47985-w#ref-CR70" id="ref-link-section-d25187e2938">70</a></sup>) implemented in SynMap<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 69" title="Lyons, E., Pedersen, B., Kane, J. &amp; Freeling, M. The value of nonmodel genomes and an example using SynMap within CoGe to dissect the hexaploidy that predates the Rosids. Trop. Plant Biol. 1, 181â190 (2008)." href="/articles/s41598-019-47985-w#ref-CR69" id="ref-link-section-d25187e2942">69</a></sup>, and used to estimate the divergence time between the four Solanaceae (Supplementary Information 2.7).</p><p>The hypothetical ancestral chromosomes of the common ancestor of pepper, tomato, potato and eggplant, using coffee as an outgroup, were based on shared genes obtained from COGE<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 69" title="Lyons, E., Pedersen, B., Kane, J. &amp; Freeling, M. The value of nonmodel genomes and an example using SynMap within CoGe to dissect the hexaploidy that predates the Rosids. Trop. Plant Biol. 1, 181â190 (2008)." href="/articles/s41598-019-47985-w#ref-CR69" id="ref-link-section-d25187e2949">69</a></sup> outputs among the five species. GRIMM-Synteny<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 71" title="Tesler, G. Efficient algorithms for multichromosomal genome rearrangements. J. Comput. Syst. Sci. 65, 587â609 (2002)." href="/articles/s41598-019-47985-w#ref-CR71" id="ref-link-section-d25187e2953">71</a></sup> was used to identify syntenic blocks among the 5 species, and were analysed with MGRA<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 72" title="Alekseyev, M. A. &amp; Pevzner, P. A. Breakpoint graphs and ancestral genome reconstructions. Genome Res. 19, 943â57 (2009)." href="/articles/s41598-019-47985-w#ref-CR72" id="ref-link-section-d25187e2957">72</a></sup> and ProCARs<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 73" title="Perrin, A., VarrÃ©, J.-S., Blanquart, S. &amp; Ouangraoua, A. ProCARs: Progressive Reconstruction of Ancestral Gene Orders. BMC Genomics 16(Suppl 5), S6 (2015)." href="/articles/s41598-019-47985-w#ref-CR73" id="ref-link-section-d25187e2961">73</a></sup> pipeline (Supplementary Information 2.7).</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec16">Gene family analyses</h3><p>The distribution of orthologous gene families was calculated using OrthoMCL<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 16" title="Li, L., Stoeckert, C. J. &amp; Roos, D. S. OrthoMCL: identification of ortholog groups for eukaryotic genomes. Genome Res. 13, 2178â89 (2003)." href="/articles/s41598-019-47985-w#ref-CR16" id="ref-link-section-d25187e2973">16</a></sup> version 2.0.9 on annotations from eggplant, pepper (PGA v1.55), tomato (iTAG v2.4), potato (iTAG v1) and Arabidopsis (TAIR10) (Supplementary InformationÂ <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41598-019-47985-w#MOESM1">2.4</a>). Orthologs were identified using CoGe<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 69" title="Lyons, E., Pedersen, B., Kane, J. &amp; Freeling, M. The value of nonmodel genomes and an example using SynMap within CoGe to dissect the hexaploidy that predates the Rosids. Trop. Plant Biol. 1, 181â190 (2008)." href="/articles/s41598-019-47985-w#ref-CR69" id="ref-link-section-d25187e2980">69</a></sup> (Supplementary Information 2.7); if not possible, putative orthologs were identified as best-hits by reciprocal BLAST (Supplementary Information 2.4).</p><p>A script developed in-house, based on a BLASTp analysis, was employed to identify eggplant (<i>Solanum melongena</i>) pathogen recognition proteins (PRPs) (Supplementary Information 3.1). The set of predicted PRPs identified was further analyzed using InterProScan<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 62" title="Jones, P. et al. InterProScan 5: genome-scale protein function classification. Bioinformatics 30, 1236â40 (2014)." href="/articles/s41598-019-47985-w#ref-CR62" id="ref-link-section-d25187e2990">62</a></sup> software. The phylogenetic relationships of Solanaceae CNL and TNL proteins was calculated separately and similarities were determined performing a MAFFT<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 74" title="Katoh, K. &amp; Standley, D. M. MAFFT multiple sequence alignment software version 7: improvements in performance and usability. Mol. Biol. Evol. 30, 772â80 (2013)." href="/articles/s41598-019-47985-w#ref-CR74" id="ref-link-section-d25187e2994">74</a></sup> (E-INS-i algorithm) multiple alignment. Clades were collapsed and numerated based on a bootstrap value over 85. Evolutionary analyses were conducted in MEGA6<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 75" title="Tamura, K., Stecher, G., Peterson, D., Filipski, A. &amp; Kumar, S. MEGA6: Molecular Evolutionary Genetics Analysis Version 6.0. Mol. Biol. Evol. 30, 2725â2729 (2013)." href="/articles/s41598-019-47985-w#ref-CR75" id="ref-link-section-d25187e2998">75</a></sup>.</p><p>The bootstrap consensus tree was inferred from 100 replicates. The PRGs cluster analysis was conducted using R software<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 76" title="R Development Core Team. R Software. R: A Language and Environment for Statistical Computing (2013)." href="/articles/s41598-019-47985-w#ref-CR76" id="ref-link-section-d25187e3005">76</a></sup>. Evolutionary relationships were inferred by using the Maximum Likelihood method based on the JTT matrix-based model<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 77" title="Jones, D. T., Taylor, W. R. &amp; Thornton, J. M. The rapid generation of mutation data matrices from protein sequences. Comput. Appl. Biosci. 8, 275â82 (1992)." href="/articles/s41598-019-47985-w#ref-CR77" id="ref-link-section-d25187e3009">77</a></sup>. Heatmaps were produced using Genesis<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 78" title="Sturn, A., Quackenbush, J. &amp; Trajanoski, Z. Genesis: cluster analysis of microarray data. Bioinformatics 18, 207â208 (2002)." href="/articles/s41598-019-47985-w#ref-CR78" id="ref-link-section-d25187e3013">78</a></sup>.</p><p>Coexpression analysis was carried out with CoExpress (<a href="http://sablab.net/coexpress.html">http://sablab.net/coexpress.html</a>) using Tomato MADS-box encoding gene RIN and its orthologs in Eggplant and in Pepper as âbaitsâ; the resulting lists of co-expressed genes which were filtered by r-valueââ¥â0.6 (Supplementary Information 3.3).</p></div></div></section>
                

                <section aria-labelledby="data-availability" data-title="Data Availability"><div class="c-article-section" id="data-availability-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="data-availability">Data Availability</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="data-availability-content">
              
              <p>The reads have been submitted to the NCBI Sequence Read Archive under the accession number SRP078398. Upon acceptance, the assembly and annotation will be made available, in downloadable form, on GenBank and the Solanaceae Genome Network. Further information, including the â67/3â genome assembly, pseudomolecules, annotations and Gbrowse are available through the website at <a href="http://www.eggplantgenome.org">www.eggplantgenome.org</a>. For reviewing purposes, access can be obtained using the following credentials: User: anonymous; Password: geite0Ja. Eggplant biological materials can be requested to G.L.R. (giuseppeleonardo.rotino@crea.gov.it) and A.Ah. (asaph.aharoni@weizmann.ac.il).</p>
